It will also greatly facilitate map-based cloning of agricultural important genes from lettuce that is required for crop improvement using genome editing, particularly those involved in resistance to abiotic and biotic stresses.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec11" data-title="Methods"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec11-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec11">Methods</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec11-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec12">Library preparation and sequencing</h3><p>Further details of all methods are presented in <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ncomms14953#MOESM3167">Supplementary Note 1</a>. DNA was extracted using a modified CTAB method<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Doyle, J. &amp; Doyle, J. L. Genomic plant DNA preparation from fresh tissue-CTAB method. Phytochem. Bull 19, 11–15 (1987)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2350">53</a></sup> from seedlings of <i>L. sativa</i> cv. Salinas grown in the dark. Seven genomic libraries were constructed with insert sizes from 170 bp to 40 kb and sequenced on the Illumina HiSeq 2000 to generate 298 Gb of raw sequence. Filtering to remove low-quality reads, adapter contamination, ambiguous bases and error correction provided 198.5 Gb of clean data for assembly.</p><p>The 99 recombinant lines (RILs) derived from <i>L. sativa</i> cv. Salinas × <i>L. serriola</i> acc. US96UC23 were a subset of the 213 RILs used to generate Affymetrix GeneChip map<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 20" title="Truco, M. J. et al. An ultra high-density, transcript-based, genetic map of Lettuce. G3 Genes Genomes Genetics 3, 617–631 (2013)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2366">20</a></sup>. Genomic DNA was isolated from leaves of the RILs using a modified CTAB extraction method<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Rogers, S. O. &amp; Bendich, A. J. in Plant Molecular Biology Manual (eds Gelvin, S. B., Schilperoort, R. A. &amp; Verma, D. P. S.) 73–83Springer Netherlands (1988)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2370">54</a></sup>. Genomic paired-end libraries were then prepared using standard procedures. Libraries were sequenced to approximately 1x on an Illumina Hiseq 2000.</p><p>Two Chicago libraries were prepared by Dovetail genomics as described previously<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="Putnam, N. H. et al. Chromosome-scale shotgun assembly using an in vitro method for long-range linkage. Genome Res. 26, 342–350 (2016)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2377">13</a></sup>. Libraries were sequenced in two lanes on an Illumina HiSeq 2500 in rapid run mode to generate 313.5 and 357.2 M 100 bp read pairs. This provided a total of 72 × physical coverage.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec13">Genome assemblies</h3><p>SOAPdenovo2 was used for initial assembly of the genomic libraries with a round of gap-filling after the scaffolds had been constructed. This assembly was used as input to the HiRise program along with data from the Chicago libraries for scaffolding using contact frequency information. After scaffolding, another round of gap-filling was done to close the gaps. Two iterations of HiRise scaffolding were done; the first used a single lane of sequencing from one Chicago library and the second used data from sequencing one lane of each two Chicago libraries made from larger DNA fragments. Completeness of the gene-space was evaluated using CEGMA, a set of 357 Ultra Conserved Ortologous Sequences and EST sequences from NCBI for <i>Lactuca</i> spp.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec14">Assembly validation and genetic analysis</h3><p>Reads for each of the 99 F<sub>7</sub> RILs were mapped to the genomic sequence of <i>L. sativa</i> using CLC Genomics Server 6.5 (Qiagen, Redwood City, CA, USA) and haplotypes assigned to each scaffold in each RIL based on the consensus all single-nucleotide polymorphisms detected per scaffold. Scaffolds that exhibited haplotypes with many discontinuities at the same position were considered to be chimeric (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ncomms14953#MOESM3167">Supplementary Fig. 1</a>); these putative chimeras were manually split and the subsections mapped independently. All scaffolds over 1 kb were clustered into nine chromosomal linkage groups using MadMapper<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Kozik, A. Suite of python MadMapper scripts for quality control of genetic markers, group analysis and inference of linear order of markers on linkage groups (2006). Available at: 
                    http://cgpdb.ucdavis.edu/XLinkage/MadMapper/
                    
                  ." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2408">55</a></sup>. Scaffolds within each chromosomal linkage group were then assigned to genetic bins based on their segregation using MSTmap<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Wu, Y., Bhat, P. R., Close, T. J. &amp; Lonardi, S. Efficient and accurate construction of genetic linkage maps from the minimum spanning tree of a graph. PLoS Genet 4, e1000212 (2008)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2412">56</a></sup>. For comparison of the new genetic map with the previous Affymetrix GeneChip map<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 20" title="Truco, M. J. et al. An ultra high-density, transcript-based, genetic map of Lettuce. G3 Genes Genomes Genetics 3, 617–631 (2013)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2417">20</a></sup> unigenes used in the chip-based map<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Stoffel, K. et al. Development and application of a 6.5 million feature Affymetrix Genechip for massively parallel discovery of single position polymorphisms in lettuce (Lactuca spp.). BMC Genomics 13, 185 (2012)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2421">57</a></sup> were mapped to the SoapDenovo assembly.</p><p>Genetic information from the map based on the SOAPdenovo scaffolds was used for validation of the HiRise superscaffolds by correlating their physical and genetic positions. After validation and clean-up of the HiRise assembly, superscaffolds were mapped into the nine LGs. An initial order was assigned based on the genetic position of the first and last scaffolds within the superscaffold; validated superscaffolds were oriented based on their terminal locations. This order was revised based in the terminal haplotypes to minimize the double recombinants and genetic inconsistencies; the refined order of the superscaffolds was used to construct chromosomal pseudomolecules joining superscaffolds with 10 kb of N’s as spacers. Telomeric sequence arrays were found by string searches of known telomere sequences.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec15">Prediction and analysis of repeat sequences</h3><p>Transposable elements were identified in the genome using a combination of homology-based and <i>de novo</i> approaches<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Li, R. et al. De novo assembly of human genomes with massively parallel short read sequencing. Genome Res. 20, 265–272 (2010)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2439">58</a></sup>. The genome was mined for repeat elements using ProteinMask and RepeatMasker<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Smit, A., Hubley, R. &amp; Green, P. RepeatMasker Open-3.0. 
                    http://www.repeatmasker.org
                    
                   (2017)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2443">59</a></sup> using Repbase<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Jurka, J. et al. Repbase Update, a database of eukaryotic repetitive elements. Cytogenet. Genome Res. 110, 462–467 (2005)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2447">60</a></sup> and a set of custom repeat libraries as reference. Additionally, TRF<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Benson, G. Tandem repeats finder: a program to analyze DNA sequences. Nucleic Acids Res. 27, 573–580 (1999)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2451">61</a></sup> was used to find tandem repeats.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec16">Prediction of non-coding RNA genes</h3><p>Prediction of ncRNA was done by type, and first tRNAscan-SE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Lowe, T. M. &amp; Eddy, S. R. tRNAscan-SE: a program for improved detection of transfer RNA genes in genomic sequence. Nucleic Acids Res. 25, 955–964 (1997)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2464">62</a></sup> was used to predict tRNAs. Similarly snoscan<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Lowe, T. M. &amp; Eddy, S. R. A computational screen for methylation guide snoRNAs in yeast. Science 283, 1168–1171 (1999)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2468">63</a></sup> and RNAmmer<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Lagesen, K. et al. RNAmmer: consistent and rapid annotation of ribosomal RNA genes. Nucleic Acids Res. 35, 3100–3108 (2007)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2472">64</a></sup> were used to predict snoRNA and rRNA, respectively. Infernal<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Nawrocki, E. P. &amp; Eddy, S. R. Infernal 1.1: 100-fold faster RNA homology searches. Bioinforma. 29, 2933–2935 (2013)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2476">65</a></sup> was used for prediction of more ncRNA using the rFam database<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Nawrocki, E. P. et al. Rfam 12.0: Updates to the RNA families database. Nucleic Acids Res. 43, D130–D137 (2015)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2480">66</a></sup> as input for miRNA, rRNA, rybozimes, snRNA and tRNA.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec17">Small RNA and target gene analysis</h3><p>Total RNA was isolated from leaves of <i>L. sativa</i> cvs. Salinas, Cobham Green and Diana, infected or not infected by <i>Bremia lactucae</i> (10 samples total). Small RNA libraries were constructed using the TruSeq Small RNA Sample Preparation Kit (Illumina, Hayward, CA, USA). Parallel analysis of RNA end (PARE) libraries were constructed as previously described<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 23" title="Zhai, J. et al. MicroRNAs as master regulators of the plant NB-LRR defense gene family via the production of phased, trans-acting siRNAs. Genes Dev. 25, 2540–2553 (2011)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2498">23</a></sup>. The libraries were sequenced on an Illumina HiSeq 2000 at the Delaware Biotechnology Institute (Newark, DE, USA).</p><p>The raw reads of sRNA sequencing data were trimmed to remove adaptor sequences and then mapped to the lettuce genome using Bowtie<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="Langmead, B., Trapnell, C., Pop, M. &amp; Salzberg, S. L. Ultrafast and memory-efficient alignment of short DNA sequences to the human genome. Genome Biol. 10, R25 (2009)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2505">67</a></sup>. Reads that matched tRNAs, rRNAs, snRNA and snoRNAs were excluded. Only reads that perfectly matched the lettuce genome were used for further study; miRNA prediction was performed using the previously reported pipeline<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Arikit, S. et al. An atlas of soybean small RNAs identifies phased siRNAs from hundreds of coding genes. Plant Cell 26, 4584–4601 (2014)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2509">25</a></sup>. <i>PHAS</i> analyses were conducted as described previously<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Arikit, S. et al. An atlas of soybean small RNAs identifies phased siRNAs from hundreds of coding genes. Plant Cell 26, 4584–4601 (2014)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2516">25</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="Xia, R. et al. MicroRNA superfamilies descended from miR390 and their roles in secondary small interfering RNA biogenesis in Eudicots. Plant Cell 25, 1555–1572 (2013)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2519">68</a></sup>. Genome-wide miRNA target prediction was performed using the sPARTA package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Kakrana, A., Hammond, R., Patel, P., Nakano, M. &amp; Meyers, B. C. sPARTA: a parallelized pipeline for integrated analysis of plant miRNA and cleaved mRNA data sets, including new miRNA target-identification software. Nucleic Acids Res. 42, e139 (2014)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2523">69</a></sup> with the built-in target-prediction module miRFerno, followed by PARE-based validation of predicted targets.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec18">Gene annotation</h3><p>Protein-coding genes were predicted using multiple gene annotation pipelines. Two sets of GLEAN predictions and one set of MAKER annotations were combined into a single pool. These data were reduced to non-redundant predictions and further filtered based on an Overlap Weighted Evidence Gene-model (OWEG) score for reliability of the predictions (S.R.-C.-W., unpublished observations). The predicted proteome and genic region were evaluated with CEGMA<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 19" title="Parra, G., Bradnam, K. &amp; Korf, I. CEGMA: a pipeline to accurately annotate core genes in eukaryotic genomes. Bioinformatics 23, 1061–1067 (2007)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2535">19</a></sup> and against the UCOS<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Kozik, A. et al. in Plant and Animal Genomes Conference XVI, P6 (2008)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2539">70</a></sup> to evaluate their completeness. Tandem gene arrays were identified using the CoGe platform as one of the SynMap<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 71" title="Lyons, E., Pedersen, B., Kane, J. &amp; Freeling, M. The value of nonmodel genomes and an example using SynMap within CoGe to dissect the hexaploidy that predates the Rosids. Trop. Plant Biol. 1, 181–190 (2008)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR71" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2543">71</a></sup> outputs.</p><p>A phylogenetic tree was constructed using sequences of predicted CEG genes using CEGMA<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 19" title="Parra, G., Bradnam, K. &amp; Korf, I. CEGMA: a pipeline to accurately annotate core genes in eukaryotic genomes. Bioinformatics 23, 1061–1067 (2007)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2550">19</a></sup> on a diverse sample of Eudicot species. Sequences were aligned on Clustal Omega. These alignments were inspected visually, concatenated and used as input into Mega<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 72" title="Kumar, S., Tamura, K., Jakobsen, I. B. &amp; Nei, M. MEGA2: molecular evolutionary genetics analysis software. Bioinforma. 17, 1244–1245 (2001)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR72" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2554">72</a></sup> to determine the best substitution model. Concatenated alignment was then used to construct a maximum likelihood tree in RAxML<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 73" title="Stamatakis, A., Ludwig, T. &amp; Meier, H. RAxML-III: a fast program for maximum likelihood-based inference of large phylogenetic trees. Bioinforma. 21, 456–463 (2005)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR73" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2558">73</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec19">Protein clustering and functional annotation</h3><p>Functional annotation of all the transcripts was done using InterProScan5<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 21" title="Jones, P. et al. InterProScan 5: genome-scale protein function classification. Bioinformatics 30, 1236–1240 (2014)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR21" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2570">21</a></sup> and KEGG Automated Annotation Service (KAAS)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 74" title="Moriya, Y., Itoh, M., Okuda, S., Yoshizawa, A. C. &amp; Kanehisa, M. KAAS: an automatic genome annotation and pathway reconstruction server. Nucleic Acids Res. 35, W182–W185 (2007)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR74" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2574">74</a></sup>. Predicted proteins were BLASTed against <i>A. thaliana</i> TAIR10 proteins with BLASTp 1 × e<sup>−10</sup> to find homologous sequences. Analysis of a set of protein families domains from Pfam database v27.0 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 75" title="Finn, R. D. et al. Pfam: the protein families database. Nucleic Acids Res. 42, D222–D230 (2014)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR75" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2582">75</a>) was done on the predicted <i>L. sativa</i> annotations and a panel of published plant genomes. Number of protein domains detected per species was analysed for abundance of particular gene families in <i>L. sativa.</i></p><p>The predicted proteome of <i>L. sativa</i> was clustered in OrthoMCL<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Fischer, S. et al. Using OrthoMCL to assign proteins to OrthoMCL-DB groups or to cluster proteomes into new ortholog groups. Curr. Protoc. Bioinforma Chapter 6, Unit 6.12.1-19. (2002)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2598">27</a></sup> with proteins from published plant genomes. Genes present in clusters that were single copy and present in all genomes were used to calculate divergence with <i>V. vinifera</i> as the reference. <i>X</i><sup>2</sup> test was performed in a subset of clusters. Using annotations from <i>L. sativa</i> clusters were classified as Receptor Like Kinases (RLKs), Nucleotide binding Leucine rich repeat Receptors (NLRs), lipooxinagenase-like (LOX-like) and subjected to further analysis. Genes present in clusters specific to <i>L. sativa</i> were used for GO enrichment analysis using Blast2GO.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec20">Analysis of synteny</h3><p>Synteny was analysed using the CoGe platform (<a href="https://genomevolution.org/">https://genomevolution.org/</a>). <i>V. vinifera</i> and <i>L. sativa</i> were used as references against 16 publicly available plant genomes including <i>C. cardunculus</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Scaglione, D. et al. The genome sequence of the outbreeding globe artichoke constructed de novo incorporating a phase-aware low-pass sequencing strategy of F1 progeny. Sci. Rep 6, 19427 (2016)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2639">9</a></sup>. Besides synteny to the two reference genomes intragenomic synteny was calculated for all Asterid genomes. For comparisons against lettuce and for the intragenomic comparisons, sequence divergence estimates between syntelogs were calculated as part of CoGe.</p><p>Triplicated blocks in the <i>L. sativa</i> genome were identified by aligning syntenic blocks to the reference and extracting regions that had at least five syntenic genes across two blocks. These blocks were visually inspected and organized into triplicated regions. Divergence between the paralogous regions was calculated using the divergence between the syntelogs within each region. This information was used to group the regions into three subgenomes. Analysis of gene contents of these triplicated regions was done first by GO enrichment analysis using Blast2GO. Additional analysis was done for four families of transcription factors (WRKY, AP2, TCP, MADS). All of the predicted genes in these families were aligned on Clustal Omega and a tree constructed using Clustal Phylogeny. In parallel, mutation rates were calculated for pairs of syntelogs at the whole gene level and also for both termini independently.</p><p>Expression data for the genes within the triplicated regions were mined from multiple RNA-seq experiments. These reads were mapped to the genome and read counts were generated for the predicted genes. Downstream analysis was done using R3.1.0 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 76" title="R Core Team. R: A Language and Environment for Statistical Computing. Available at 
                    https://www.r-project.org
                    
                  ." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR76" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2651">76</a>) to normalize the raw counts with the DESeq package and then input to the Weighted Gene Correlation-Expression Network Analysis package for network construction.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec21">Data availability</h3><p>Annotated version of the genome assembly is available from NCBI Genebank under project PRJNA173551 and CoGe<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 71" title="Lyons, E., Pedersen, B., Kane, J. &amp; Freeling, M. The value of nonmodel genomes and an example using SynMap within CoGe to dissect the hexaploidy that predates the Rosids. Trop. Plant Biol. 1, 181–190 (2008)." href="/articles/ncomms14953#ref-CR71" id="ref-link-section-d2878e2663">71</a></sup> (Organism ID 36218, Genome ID 28333). All raw reads for <i>L. sativa</i> cv. Salinas have been deposited at the NCBI Sequence Read Archive (SRA) under umbrella project PRJNA173551, accession SRP105354. Sequence for all 99 F<sub>7</sub> RILs have been deposited under umbrella project PRJNA243095, accession SRP040749. Small RNA and PARE data have been deposited at the NCBI Gene Expression Omnibus (GEO) under accession GSE84280. Genome browsers and additional information of the assembly and annotation are available at <a href="http://lgr.genomecenter.ucdavis.edu">http://lgr.genomecenter.ucdavis.edu</a>. Additional information is available upon request from the corresponding author.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec22" data-title="Additional information"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec22-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec22">Additional information</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec22-content"><p><b>How to cite this article:</b> Reyes-Chin-Wo, S. <i>et al</i>. Genome assembly with <i>in vitro</i> proximity ligation data and whole-genome triplication in lettuce. <i>Nat. Commun.</i> <b>8,</b> 14953 doi: 10.1038/ncomms14953 (2017).</p><p><b>Publisher’s note:</b> Springer Nature remains neutral with regard to jurisdictional claims in published maps and institutional affiliations.</p></div></div></section>
